  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText10784775344995855752" style="display:none">'She stood in Purgatory and studied death. The blood and the gore of it, the ferocity of its glee. It had come to this place with the wilful temper of a child, full of heat and passion and careless brutality.' <br /><br />In an uptown strip joint a cop is found bludgeoned to death. The weapon's a baseball bat. The motive is a mystery. It's a case of serious overkill that pushes Eve Dallas straight into overdrive. Her investigation uncovers a private club that's more than a hot spot. Purgatory's a last chance for atonement where everyone is judged. Where your ultimate fate depends on your most intimate sins. And where one cop's hidden secrets are about to plunge innocent souls into vice-ridden damnation...</span>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1431163-can-anyone-tell-me-the-exact-place-in-the"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Can anyone tell me the exact place in the book where she realizes it's Clooney? And the exact place where Captain Roth does something specifically so egregious that she now is getting "a six-month probationary period before they decide if she keeps her command." I might have been sleeping/ watching The Voice (LOL) as these parts came into play, but I sure missed them. I saw it coming. Then bam...Eve goes to Clooney. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/23051669-julie-ann"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1604635057i/23051669._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/23051669-julie-ann">Julie Ann</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Chapter 19 reread the beginning and the end. I know I missed this when I first read the book, but did catch on my reread. "But something had rooted in<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Chapter 19 reread the beginning and the end. I know I missed this when I first read the book, but did catch on my reread. "But something had rooted in her brain, something that had her leapfrogging over the current data and running yet another search." She gets called to Tibbles office and has Peabody finish the run. At the end of the chapter Peabody reports on the run. Probability 76% "but the computer doesn't count grief or mind games." says Eve. As far as Captain Roth, I agree the previous answer. She had not noticed many of the things going on in her department. Chapter 11 we hear her alibi and personal problems when Eve is questioning her. She is ordered to give a report on her division when Tibble, Whitney, Bayless, Roth, Fenney and Eve meet in Chapter 13. Chapter 16 - Eve is doing runs on people with Roarke's computer. Roth's life story, marital problems and self paid counseling is accurate. Eve states/predicts "She won't keep her squad command when all this washes down." In Chapter 19 Eve interviews Vernon, another bad cop. He is naming many names, so more dirt is surfacing. Whitney said both he and Tibble would be watching the interrogation of Vernon, when she requested the warrant on Bayliss. Martinez is the one to tell Eve about Roth getting slapped on record, required to do counseling, and 6 month probationary period - Chapter 22.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1828018157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1828018157" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1828018157?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749956219" href="/book/show/12735370-judgement-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1828018157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18354655332724745613">Over the course of this long series I am always amazed at the consistent quality of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb' title='J.D. Robb' rel='nofollow noopener'>J.D. Robb</a>'s writing, but some of the books do stand out in excellence. This is one of them. <br/>There is everything in this book!<br/>Nearly all of our favourite characters make an appearance. Mavis has a very funny scene with Eve when they try to solve her problems with the aid of alcohol and ice cream. Mira tries to help solve the same problems in a very different way. Summerset only has less than a page but makes a rea</span>
  <span id="freeText18354655332724745613" style="display:none">Over the course of this long series I am always amazed at the consistent quality of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb" title="J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">J.D. Robb</a>'s writing, but some of the books do stand out in excellence. This is one of them. <br />There is everything in this book!<br />Nearly all of our favourite characters make an appearance. Mavis has a very funny scene with Eve when they try to solve her problems with the aid of alcohol and ice cream. Mira tries to help solve the same problems in a very different way. Summerset only has less than a page but makes a real impact. His relationship with Eve is developing nicely:) <br />The action is full on and there are plenty of murders and the resultant police work. Eve is on top of her game and never falters despite constant interference from various sources.<br />The humour of course is always there. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17065.J_D__Robb" title="J.D. Robb" rel="nofollow noopener">J.D. Robb</a> has a talent for funny one liners and amusing banter.<br />I do have issues with Roarke in this book because I felt he was way out of line when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he interfered in Eve's case. He did ambush her by going to her bosses behind her back.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Not one of his better moments but I guess the man is human.<br />I love this series:)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18354655332724745613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I mean, it's a lot of work to catch a killer and he is kinda helping clean-up the police department.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469828666i/19862873._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Okay, okay. Killing is wrong. blah.blah.blah.<br><br>Along with this mystery is the mystery of Eve's stolen candy. She still hasn't caught the thief who is stealing her candy and actually had to resort to eating an apple. Why, God, why? Life can be so cruel. Of course, I have my suspicions about who the candy-thief is and hope to have them confirmed in the future. <br><br>And, really, that is the fun in these books because it's not that hard to figure out the bad-guy usually, but watching all of it play out is good. Finding out why they did it and all of the other details is fun.<br><br>There is also trouble in paradise. Eve and Roarke get into a serious knock-down, drag-out fight in this book. I'm hoping that they break up and Roarke needs comforting in the arms of an older, chubbier woman. I'll be waiting...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469828666i/19862874.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6889572463994841484"><br/>LOVED IT. It is as simple as that. This series is crazy good. I’m still baffled as to how she does it.   <span id="freeText6889572463994841484" style="display:none"><br>LOVED IT. It is as simple as that. This series is crazy good. I’m still baffled as to how she does it. After 11 books I still adore Roarke and Eve. <br><br>In <b>Judgement in Death</b> cops are being murdered. One is murdered in a place Roarke owns. Eve is not surprised by this but this particular club connects Roarke to a man he thought he left in his past. Max Ricker would make a mistake that he’d regret.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486687682i/21941065._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i> Listen to me now, and carefully. Touch her, put your hand on what’s mine again, and I’ll follow you to hell and peel the skin from your bones. I’ll feed you your own eyes. I take an oath on it. Remember what I was, and you’ll know I’ll do it. And worse.” He straightened again, his body rigid. “Get someone to drag him out of here. This is my place.”</i>
</blockquote> <br><br>Eve always puts herself in the throes of things. It is who she is and how she does her job. It is what makes her so good. Roarke’s love for her runs deep but it isn’t always easy for him to keep things in check.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486687682i/21941066._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Life has very little even ground.” But he couldn’t hold out against her misery and stopped halfway down the stairs. “I love you, Eve. Nothing changes that, nothing could. But Christ, you piss me off.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Telling a lie even if it is for all the right reasons will never sit well with Roarke. But Eve thinks she is doing the right thing when she decides to keep something from him…..that is until he finds out. Navigating through marriage is hard enough for her. When Roarke freezes her out she has no clue what to do. Then after a night of drinking, who would have thought that Mavis would give her the best advice? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486688068i/21941086._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Dallas.” Mavis leaned over, then slid gracefully to the floor. “You didn’t figure the man factor. They got dicks. You can’t ever forget the dick when you’re dealing with a man.” <br><br>“Because women work on an emotional level.” Mavis hiccuped delicately. “Even you.” Eve rolled over, eyed Mavis narrowly. “Do not.” <br><br>“Do, too. First, he got you by the hormones. I mean, Jesus, look at him. The man’s a sexual . . . Gimme minute. A sexual . . . banquet. Yeah, that’s a good one. Then he clicked into your head, because he’s smart and interesting and mysterious and all that stuff you’d really go for. But then, the whammer was when he jammed right into your heart. Whatcha gonna do then? A guy got his hooks in your heart, he just reels you right in.” <br><br> “I’m not a goddamn fish.” <br><br>“We are all fish,” Mavis said in rounded tones, “in the great sea of life.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>It was a battle for Eve. For the longest time work was her life. It was all she knew. Roarke was now part of her life and when these two pieces crashed together it was hard for her. But loving Roarke filled the emptiness in her heart. He was becoming her everything. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486688351i/21941099.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i> Marriage, Eve thought as she took her seat, was a puzzle she didn’t think she’d ever solve. Too many damn pieces. And the shapes of them were constantly changing on her.<br>She started out, glanced back. Roarke was still watching her, the faintest of smiles on that killer mouth, the faintest glint in those wild blue eyes. “Jesus, he makes your mouth water.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I am definitely addicted to this series. I can't seem to get enough of Roarke and Eve. All of the side characters continue to wow me too. Feeney, McNab and Peabody. And of course, Summerset, Mavis and Mira too!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486688351i/21941100._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote> <i>“Look, there’s some whattayacallems.” <br>“Daffodils,” he said and caught her hand in his. <br>“Daffodils, Eve. It’s spring.”<br> “Finally feels like it, too.”</i>
</blockquote><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9615945774110845057"><i>Judgment in Death</i> is #11 in the In Death series, and a re-read for me. My love of this series continues – I would say it’s the best series I’ve ever read (my personal opinion of course!) Author JD Robb seems to have unlimited ideas for this series, and I hope she never runs out!<br/><br/>For Detective Eve Dallas, this case is far too personal. Cops dying, being brutally murdered one after the other – the rage of the killer was obvious; the little constants always there. Eve, with the help of the whole NYP</span>
  <span id="freeText9615945774110845057" style="display:none"><i>Judgment in Death</i> is #11 in the In Death series, and a re-read for me. My love of this series continues – I would say it’s the best series I’ve ever read (my personal opinion of course!) Author JD Robb seems to have unlimited ideas for this series, and I hope she never runs out!<br /><br />For Detective Eve Dallas, this case is far too personal. Cops dying, being brutally murdered one after the other – the rage of the killer was obvious; the little constants always there. Eve, with the help of the whole NYPSD – and Roarke – were determined to get answers. <br /><br />Another excellent read; the laugh out loud moments are there; the seriousness of murder; the antics between Roarke and Eve – all together make a highly recommendable series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11373219434051814736">This is my third time reading straight through the In Death series (have read certain books many times more), and I have to say it is pure pleasure each time.   <span id="freeText11373219434051814736" style="display:none">This is my third time reading straight through the In Death series (have read certain books many times more), and I have to say it is pure pleasure each time. I first read the paperbacks, then had the pleasure of listening to Susan Ericksen's interpretation in the audiobooks, and now - this time, I'm reading them on Kindle. Never gets old. Judgement is a favorite for all the Roarke and Eve scenes as I'm a big fan of the character relationship development in the series. The supporting cast is awesome, as always, and the murder mystery intriguing. If you haven't tried this series, you're missing a real gem. It's nearly impossible to keep a series fresh book after book after book and yet, Robb knocks it out of the park every single time. Another Must Read in the series!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391985179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7512400414632017156">5 blazing Stars!!<br/><br/>One of the best installments in the series (or maybe it is just me because it's been a while since I had a session with the gang.) <br/><br/>Have I told you how amazing Eve is? In all aspects of her life? She is a woman who has a working brain in that beautiful head of hers. It is uncommon in fiction, but this heroine actually THINKS. <br/>As a cop, she doens't leave one angle unexplored, she actually has a knack for getting into any perpetrator's brain and anticipate his every move. In this b</span>
  <span id="freeText7512400414632017156" style="display:none">5 blazing Stars!!<br /><br />One of the best installments in the series (or maybe it is just me because it's been a while since I had a session with the gang.) <br /><br />Have I told you how amazing Eve is? In all aspects of her life? She is a woman who has a working brain in that beautiful head of hers. It is uncommon in fiction, but this heroine actually THINKS. <br />As a cop, she doens't leave one angle unexplored, she actually has a knack for getting into any perpetrator's brain and anticipate his every move. In this book's case she was after a cop-killer, which in itself is a very emotional and demanding task. I'm proud to state that I had figured out the killer from the start, but knowing this didn't decrease my enjoyment of the story. It was really fun to pay attention to every clue the author left and how smart Eve was to grab it. Applause to both J.D. Robb and Eve. Someone would think that the author might get sloppy or hasty after so many books, but NO, this one was as solid a mystery as in any previous book in the series.<br />As a friend, she is loyal, always standing by her friends or whomever is decent and fair towards her. But be cautious, if you ever cross her or betray her!<br />As a wife, it is a delight to watch her toss her hard skin and become vulnerable towards her husband, to open up her heart to potential pain, in order to feel love's warming to maximum. In this story, Eve and Roarke often collide (as they usually do) but it was a pleasant surprise to see, for once, that Eve was the one to humble herself first, admit the wrongness of her behavior and reach out to Roarke. The magnitude of her love for Roarke and the amount of progress she has done in their relationship, literally stuns me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7512400414632017156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332170769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14037247719951740692"><i>Thirty pieces of silver.</i><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1421215984p8/1121770.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>★★★★★ & a W.O.W! (This is a review of the audiobook.) I feel like a parrot, because I keep saying this, but this series just keeps getting better and better. This is certainly due, in large part, to <b>Susan Ericksen</b>’s excellent narration. She knows these characters so well and is so versatile with the voices. Love the rugged, poetic Irish lilt of Roarke’s voice; the friendly airiness of Mavis’s; the professional, dependable, but decidedly sassy Detective Delia Peabody’s; a</span>
  <span id="freeText14037247719951740692" style="display:none"><i>Thirty pieces of silver.</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1421215984p8/1121770.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>★★★★★ &amp; a W.O.W! (This is a review of the audiobook.) I feel like a parrot, because I keep saying this, but this series just keeps getting better and better. This is certainly due, in large part, to <b>Susan Ericksen</b>’s excellent narration. She knows these characters so well and is so versatile with the voices. Love the rugged, poetic Irish lilt of Roarke’s voice; the friendly airiness of Mavis’s; the professional, dependable, but decidedly sassy Detective Delia Peabody’s; and the insightful, intelligence, serene, upper class New England accent of Dr. Charlotte Mira’s.<br> <br>Still, I have to give Ms. Robb (AKA Nora Roberts) major kudos. It is hard to maintain a series and keep it fresh and interesting – and have the two main characters married! Each book contains a well-developed mystery, plus continues with an evolution of her passionate, powerful protagonists and her amazing secondary characters. It is fun to get to know them all, and neat to see they do something totally in character – <b>yet somehow surprising</b>! It takes a deft hand to do that.<br> <br>In this one, she concentrates on the relationship between Roarke and Eve and all I can say is “O.M.G!” repeatedly. Ms. Robb pushes the envelope, takes them to a new level, and makes it work – all while entwining them in a compelling mystery that is the catalyst of their evolution.<br><i><br>In Death series in correct reading order.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3062830.Naked_in_Death__In_Death___1_" title="Naked in Death (In Death, #1) by J.D. <div id="review_473899210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473899210" />
    <a title="Aly is so frigging bored" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored"><img alt="Aly is so frigging bored" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574767515p2/4290492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473899210?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly is so frigging bored" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly is so frigging bored" href="/user/show/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored">Aly is so frigging bored</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473899210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15935145923083332449">2nd read: 27th November-1st december 2014<br/><br/><br/>1st read: 26th February- 13th March 2013<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/XAPjqBg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400312i/775551._SY540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>That's me every time I finish a book in this series</i><br/>This is the first installment in the <b>In death</b> series that I review, and it’s hard! I loved everything, even the fighting, and I don’t have anything to say that the other people who wrote reviews didn’t say before me. It was a pleasure to listen to it, I don’t think I’ve enjoyed another audiobook more. <br/><br/>About the novel: In this book Eve deals with a cop killer and</span>
  <span id="freeText15935145923083332449" style="display:none">2nd read: 27th November-1st december 2014<br><br><br>1st read: 26th February- 13th March 2013<br><a href="http://imgur.com/XAPjqBg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400312i/775551._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>That's me every time I finish a book in this series</i><br>This is the first installment in the <b>In death</b> series that I review, and it’s hard! I loved everything, even the fighting, and I don’t have anything to say that the other people who wrote reviews didn’t say before me. It was a pleasure to listen to it, I don’t think I’ve enjoyed another audiobook more. <br><br>About the novel: In this book Eve deals with a cop killer and as you can imagine Roarke gets involved(being awesome and owning half the universe or more he really can’t help it). I had moments when I thought that I knew who the unsub was, but then I convinced myself that I was wrong… Ms. Robb has such great talent that she manages to make you doubt everything, you can’t find that in many writers. She plays us, readers, like a virtuoso and drops hints and facts when you don’t expect it and you start being unsure again and again. <br>This book had something that the others from the series didn’t: a fight, a big one, between Eve and Roarke! I hated every minute of it, of not seeing them being the perfect couple I knew they were, of them not showing their trust and love in each other as they always did… But I also loved it(I know… I know… I can’t make my mind up). Ms. Robb showed us that she created real characters with real feelings and not some plastic puppets that you get bored of and despise in the end. I loved how she made everything work, and… let’s face it: I loved the making up part =))<br>The secondary characters that we’ve come to expect were also here and had minor and major roles and we saw more glimpses from their lives: Peabody still strings McNab along and loves it, Doctor Mira is the strong professional woman that, to me, shows how Eve will be in 20 something years and how well hers and Roarke’s relationship will go, Mavis and Leonardo have the time of their lives together and with their careers… all in all: everything is well when it ends well. <br><a href="http://imgur.com/WTc79GU" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400312i/775552.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>About the narrator: Susan Ericksen is a goddess! I want to marry her and never let her go! She makes all the characters unique that you know them and she gets all the accents and nuances right! I wish she will do all the audiobooks in the world, or at least those I listen to!<br><br><br>Quotes(the best of the best):<br>"You know the problem of seeing 2 guys?"<br>"What is it Peabody?"<br>"There isn't one!"(Eve and Peabody)<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Eve's mouth fell open. "Stupid? You're saying I was stupid? You're supposed to tell me I was right. That's how this works."<br>"Dallas." Mavis leaned over, then slid gracefully to the floor. "You didn't figure the man factor. They got dicks. You can't ever forget the dick when you're dealing with a man."<br>"What're you talking about?" Eve slid to the floor as well, sucked down the rest of her drink. "I know Roarke has a dick. He uses it every chance he gets."<br>"The dick's connected to the ego. It's medical fact. Or maybe it's the other way around." With a shrug, Mavis emptied the last of the screamers. "It's a mystery to all womankind. You didn't trust him to handle himself."<br>"He didn't trust me to handle myself."<br>"Dallas, Dallas." Shaking her head, Mavis patted Eve's thigh. "Dallas," she said a third time, with great pity. "Let's make more screamers. We'll need them when we get to the men are pigs stage."(Eve and Mavis)<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>"Nonetheless. Both of you reacted as natural for you, engaged in a bout of rough, sweaty sex that no doubt satisfied you."<br>"You'd have thought so, but we hadn't even cooled off when he picked me up off the floor and carried me into bed and did it all over again."<br>Mira stared, rather blankly. "Does he have a particular diet? Vitamins?"(Mira and Eve)<br><br><br>"You pulled your weapon on me." He couldn't get over that one. Wasn't sure he ever would.<br>"That's right." She shoved his hand away from her chin. "You think I'm stupid enough to jump physically between two crazy men trying to break each other's faces? I had it on stun."<br>"Oh, well then, what am I whining about? You had it on stun." He had to laugh. "Christ, Eve."<br>"I wouldn't have used it on you. Probably. And if I had, I'd've been really sorry."(Eve and Roarke)<br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_385262952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385262952" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470503541p2/11382577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385262952?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=strong-female-characters">strong-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11382577-kristen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385262952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14935425041910827839">I'm still completely and unapologetically addicted to the characters in this series - especially Eve and Roarke, but even the supporting characters are so real and relatable they get under my skin.<br/><br/>This time around, Eve's hunting a cop killer. A cop killer who seems to be killing cops who may or may not be on the take. Naturally, cops don't like to be investigated, especially by another cop, so Eve's not too popular - but, being Eve, that makes no difference at all to her doing what she has to do</span>
  <span id="freeText14935425041910827839" style="display:none">I'm still completely and unapologetically addicted to the characters in this series - especially Eve and Roarke, but even the supporting characters are so real and relatable they get under my skin.<br /><br />This time around, Eve's hunting a cop killer. A cop killer who seems to be killing cops who may or may not be on the take. Naturally, cops don't like to be investigated, especially by another cop, so Eve's not too popular - but, being Eve, that makes no difference at all to her doing what she has to do.<br /><br />But just to add another layer of complication, there's a criminal type somehow mixed up in what's going on, who just happens to be a former associate of Roarke's from before he went on the straight and narrow, and he's crazy as well as dangerous because he wants revenge on Roarke and he has no problem at all using Eve to get that revenge.<br /><br />Although I enjoy the murder investigations, the irresistible draw of the series for me are the characters. There's a reason why Nora Roberts - writing as J.D. Robb - has published so many books and is consistently on bestseller lists - she writes amazing characters doing interesting things in ways that make you want to be IN the books!<br /><br />Even the supporting and minor characters in this series are written as fully realized people. You feel like you really know these people, whether you like them or not, so the book feels real, and you can completely dive into and experience the story, which is exactly what a great book SHOULD do for you.<br /><br />Can't wait to read the next book in this fantastic series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14935425041910827839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3436959449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3436959449" />
    <a title="Lakshmi C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7678185-lakshmi-c"><img alt="Lakshmi C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540966168p2/7678185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3436959449?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lakshmi C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lakshmi C" href="/user/show/7678185-lakshmi-c">Lakshmi C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3436959449&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3436959449" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18074484246996698280">This was an interesting murder investigation where cops are the murder victims and Eve has to figure out why. The twist in the tale - crooked cops. The investigations and it's angles - who did it and why were fun, not spoiling those.<br/><br/>Did I guess who did it? Yes.<br/>It's fun when this happens but I still like reading how Eve and Roarke trap the killer, collect evidence or trap suspects. <br/><br/>What stood out for me? <br/>I'm enjoying seeing how the characters and their relationships evolve, change over time, over</span>
  <span id="freeText18074484246996698280" style="display:none">This was an interesting murder investigation where cops are the murder victims and Eve has to figure out why. The twist in the tale - crooked cops. The investigations and it's angles - who did it and why were fun, not spoiling those.<br /><br />Did I guess who did it? Yes.<br />It's fun when this happens but I still like reading how Eve and Roarke trap the killer, collect evidence or trap suspects. <br /><br />What stood out for me? <br />I'm enjoying seeing how the characters and their relationships evolve, change over time, over cases.<br /><br />1 This book had a subplot about the challenges women face peofessionally, especially in male dominated fields.<br /><br />2 Eve's Girl gang<br />Mavis is mature and a relationship coach for Eve in this one. I like understated Mavis. Eve is slowly opening up and leaning on others for support. <br />Nadine has moved from pushy to supportive. The tentative friendship is more believable.<br />Peabody is wonderful as always.<br /><br />3 I loved the scene with Dr Mira. <br /><br />. However much it may discomfort you, Eve, I look on you as a kind of surrogate daughter. It's a pity that causes you embarrassment," she said mildly when that emotion ran over Eve's face. "You don't know my children, but I can promise you that they would tell you I am relentless when concerned about their happiness. While I will try not to interfere, I will know the cause."<br /><br />Dr Mira is epic in this scene. The mother daughter dynamic is openly acknowledged here. Eve deserves someone so supportive and perceptive.<br /><br />4 Boy Girl Dynamics <br /><br />You dented his ego, always a tricky proposition with a man, particularly a man like him. Then, before he could come to full terms with it, he walks in on you being hit on by another man."<br /><br />5 The Mother in law factor<br /><br />"Lieutenant."<br />She shoved her arms into the jacket, snarled at him. "What, goddamn it?"<br />He didn't so much as blink. "Regarding your actions of last evening—"<br />"Don't you start on me, hatchet-face." She shoved by him, wrenched open the doors.<br />"I believe," he continued in the same mild tone, "those actions were quite correct<br /><br />What I didn't like or maybe an unpopular opinion : <br /><br />Possibility of a Rant. You have been warned.<br /><br />Does anybody think Roarke and Eve got married too soon? <br /><br />They had a serious fight in this book. Issue - Actions without consulting spouse.<br />Roarke went silent and declared a Cold war. For a long time.<br />What does this solve? <br />It just keeps Eve in misery with zero effort.<br /><br />Roarke has done this before. This is turning into a mock trial.<br />1 Over the diamond necklace.<br />2 Over commitment<br />3 Over Magdalena<br /><br />I'm just 10 - 15 books in, there must be more. <br /><br />Issue - Romantic pasts.<br /><br />Eve had one ex to worry about. We meet Don in this book. He's smart, entertaining and likeable. Still has feelings for Eve.<br />Roarke and Don have a mini fight but it was not convincing. It made no impact.<br />Roarke has no fear of losing Eve.<br /><br />It's like a bite sized Toblerone. Who does it satisfy? <br /><br />Roarke has a parade of glamorous, sophisticated exes in every other book and the comparison is inevitable. Eve is insecure and subjected to this over and over. Even if Eve is a jerk at times, it's sad.<br /><br />I liked the earlier books where Eve could go back home, to her own space and relax. Now she's running from one war zone to the next - active murder investigation to marriage troubles. <br /><br />It's unbalanced somehow. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18074484246996698280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1809841924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809841924" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387526203p2/4731410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809841924?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749956219" href="/book/show/12735370-judgement-in-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=female-detectives">female-detectives</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809841924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7099068358444342305"><b>Judgement in Death</b><br/>4 Stars<br/><br/>Homicide Lieutenant Eve Dallas faces one of her most challenging cases when an off duty police officer is killed in a deliberate and vicious attack. As Eve unravels the clues, she is forced to confront the harsh realities of corruption within the force as well as cope with her husband's protective instincts. <br/><br/>The storyline revolving around the murders of several apparently corrupt police officers and their connection to a career criminal and former associate of Roarke's i</span>
  <span id="freeText7099068358444342305" style="display:none"><b>Judgement in Death</b><br />4 Stars<br /><br />Homicide Lieutenant Eve Dallas faces one of her most challenging cases when an off duty police officer is killed in a deliberate and vicious attack. As Eve unravels the clues, she is forced to confront the harsh realities of corruption within the force as well as cope with her husband's protective instincts. <br /><br />The storyline revolving around the murders of several apparently corrupt police officers and their connection to a career criminal and former associate of Roarke's is very compelling. While the details of the case initially come across as rather convoluted, everything ultimately comes together smoothly, and the culprit, although not immediately obvious, is easily pinpointed by process of elimination. <br /><br />Roarke and Eve's developing dynamic is particularly gripping in this installment as he struggles to reconcile his ego and need to protect Eve with the knowledge that she too is trying to protect him. Their power plays lead to some intense cavemen like tactics on his part, but also to some funny and sweet moments between the couple. <br /><br />The secondary cast is as appealing as ever and my favorite scene has to be Eve's conversation with Dr. Mira about Roarke, which gets the prim and proper psychologist very hot and bothered, lol! <br /><br />IAB Lieutenant Don Webster also puts in a more significant appearance and his character really shines through. One cannot help but sympathize with his situation and appreciate his honesty and candor. <br /><br />In sum, this is certainly one of the best books in the series and kudos to Robb for being able to keep her stories and characters lively and fresh for so long. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7099068358444342305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3120724155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3120724155" />
    <a title="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17755575-wendy-sthoughts"><img alt="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378340325p2/17755575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3120724155?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy&#39;sThoughts" href="/user/show/17755575-wendy-sthoughts">Wendy&#39;sThoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6699943-judgment-in-death">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">J.D. Robb Fans, Mystery, Romance</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3120724155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14465946446412805272"><b>5 I Can't Stop Reading Robb Stars<br/>* * * * * <i>Spoiler Free</i><br/>As a dedicated romance reader with a past history of mystery/thriller for years...this series is nirvana for me. It fulfills everything I love about stories and the process of reading. It keeps my mind engaged and my heart full. This is a powerful combination and Robb has hit the Mother Lode in balancing out these elements. To have a series first published in 1995 and continuing to this day...<br/>Staggering.<br/><br/>Because I have come to this series lat</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14465946446412805272" style="display:none"><b>5 I Can't Stop Reading Robb Stars<br>* * * * * <i>Spoiler Free</i><br>As a dedicated romance reader with a past history of mystery/thriller for years...this series is nirvana for me. It fulfills everything I love about stories and the process of reading. It keeps my mind engaged and my heart full. This is a powerful combination and Robb has hit the Mother Lode in balancing out these elements. To have a series first published in 1995 and continuing to this day...<br>Staggering.<br><br>Because I have come to this series late, I am able to binge read, going from the first book until the last. The only thing that can hold me back will be time and of course, finances, hahahahahha. But how wonderful I do not have to enjoy them only twice a year...the publishing pattern of the series. <br><br>In Judgment in Death, we have the continuing conflict of Eve's job as a New York City police homicide lieutenant with her husband, Roarke's numerous holding throughout the literal world. Once again, her case has Roarke's ownership of the location in play. <br><br>But this time, there is even more than just the location. </b>This time Roarke's past association with an underlord comes too close to comfort for Eve. The murder of a cop in Roarke's club is the start of a multi-layered investigation that will reveal a very deep dirty section of the NYPD.<br><br>This was a page-turner and I didn't figure out who the culprit was until the beginning of the last half. This had so much going on with multiple crossing of relationships and insights into the human mind. <br><br>One of the biggest draws in this book was the conflicts between Eve and Roarke. These people are not perfect; they are stubborn and do not give in easily. BUT they communicate...Roarke better than Eve. She is new to sharing her vulnerabilities and is scares her when the love she has for Roarke overwhelms her. She sometimes reacts in ways where she wants to protect him, only to cause more trouble in the relationship. She is learning what needs to be in a marriage and it is sometimes a hard learning curve for both of them.<br><br>The way they communicate, the dialogue between them during their most intimate emotional moments...there is a beauty captured in how it is done...just a sentence here, a moment there...It touches so deeply.<br><br>Roarke is Stunning in this. His love for Eve and his need to take hold of the main issues gives us more of him in action. He is very involved in this book in many ways and I was all for it.<br><br>The range of characters continued to hold their own; Peabody with McNab, Feeny, and now Webster. All the crew is here and we feel as we are part of this crew too. Each of these characters plays an important part. They allow some comic relief, insight to Eve and the people around her.<br><br>There is another element that is genius in the way Robb structures these books. She ends each book abruptly and references more about the last book at start of the next...So this practice makes the reader wanting what the next book is so that they can see what additional outcomes happened with Roarke and Eve. <br><br>Are they cliffhangers...not in the usual way but this practice does emotionally tie you to the next book before you even read it...A Very Smart Practice, Ms. Robb.<br><br><b>~~~~~ Before Reading ~~~~~</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Continuing my journey with Eve, Roarke, and Robb!</i>
</b><br><br><strong>For more Reviews, Free E-books and Giveaways</strong><br><div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_9267277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9267277" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/627337-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261273615p2/627337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9267277?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/627337-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9267277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2682257671982583470">This is the 11th book in the In Death series.<br/><br/>It is early Spring 2059 and Eve is called to the scene of a bludgeoning death in a classy, upscale strip club called Purgatory. The condition of the body is a testament to a rage kill and scattered amongst the remains are 30 pieces of silver.<br/><br/>Eve learns that the dead man was a cop and had once been a part of a police task force formed to put away a notorious criminal. But evidence was compromised, the case disintegrated and the criminal got away.<br/><br/>There </span>
  <span id="freeText2682257671982583470" style="display:none">This is the 11th book in the In Death series.<br /><br />It is early Spring 2059 and Eve is called to the scene of a bludgeoning death in a classy, upscale strip club called Purgatory. The condition of the body is a testament to a rage kill and scattered amongst the remains are 30 pieces of silver.<br /><br />Eve learns that the dead man was a cop and had once been a part of a police task force formed to put away a notorious criminal. But evidence was compromised, the case disintegrated and the criminal got away.<br /><br />There is an obvious connection as other cops from the same precinct are found murdered. Now Eve has to find a cop killer, face off with a master criminal and butt heads with Internal Affairs as she begins to uncover some unsavory facts about members of the force.<br /><br />As this series goes on, each book builds on the one before it. We see Eve and Roarke settle into life as a newly married couple. We watch as Eve slowly begins to remember more about her past. We learn, along with Eve, more about Roarke's own colorful unsavory past. And we enjoy Eve as she begins to slowly, accidentally build a network of friends who also become her surrogate family.<br /><br />As such, the series as a whole is enjoyable, solid and satisfies those of us who like to revisit familiar characters in a serial fashion. As in any series, not every book is uniform in content, plotting or interest. However some stand out from the others. In this series, I'd have to say I have about five or six of the books that just do it for me. They hit on all cylinders; plot, character development, humor, pathos, emotional storytelling. This is one of them.<br /><br />First we have a good crime story. The cop killers, the allusion to Judas, the slow unfolding of the depth of the corruption in force. This one was tightly written, well plotted and for once, kept me guessing.<br /><br />Second, there was a truly interesting villain. Ricker, the crime lord was a good adversary for Eve. I love the fact that he was just totally bat-shit insane. He had everyone around him so cowed, but in his relations with Eve he was Wile E. Coyote, except crazier, meaner and in a good suit. And bonus points for his deep, crazy hatred of Roarke.<br /><br />Third, great little throw away moments of humor. Eve's reactions as she questioned the stripper (she was from Utumwa Iowa and said 'Golly') were vintage Eve. It is always fun when the decidedly gritty, urban Eve Dallas is confronted with anyone or anything that is even remotely rural or suburban. She's totally freaked out and simply can't cope. Other smile-out-loud moments include Dr. Mira's reactions to Eve's vivid descriptions of the mid-argument angry sex she and Roarke indulge in. Or when McNabb generously shares his wild grape bubblegum with Roarke and the two men chew while watching their women work a grisly crime scene.<br /><br />And lastly, the great confrontation scene in Purgatory between Roarke and Ricker was worth the price of the book. Again, we see that Roarke is no simple romance novel hero. The guy is scary. And I LOVED the descriptions of the club. I could easily envision the railings that are snakes swallowing each other's tales, the dark blue mist that swirls on the dance floor, the gilded cages atop pedestals for the dancers and the hologram panther that stalks around the crowded dance floor and roars at the gyrating throng only to have them roar back. In my NYC club kid days I'd've totally lived at a club like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2682257671982583470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_661330569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661330569" />
    <a title="Andree" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2863963-andree"><img alt="Andree" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andree" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andree" href="/user/show/2863963-andree">Andree</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863963-andree?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661330569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2034215726649465485">Oh, I have mixed feelings about this one...<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I loved the Eve/Sommerset scene. I love that he took Eve's side and told her she was completely right in the actions she took to protect Roarke. I loved the scene between Even and Mira where Mira gave her relationship advice and told her she was like a surrogate daughter. That was gold. Peabody continues to be awesome. As does Feeney. Most of the cop stuff was pretty great. Even Tibble and Witney.<br/><br/>AND TWO BOOKS IN A ROW THAT DO NOT INVOLVE</span></span>
  <span id="freeText2034215726649465485" style="display:none">Oh, I have mixed feelings about this one...<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I loved the Eve/Sommerset scene. I love that he took Eve's side and told her she was completely right in the actions she took to protect Roarke. I loved the scene between Even and Mira where Mira gave her relationship advice and told her she was like a surrogate daughter. That was gold. Peabody continues to be awesome. As does Feeney. Most of the cop stuff was pretty great. Even Tibble and Witney.<br /><br />AND TWO BOOKS IN A ROW THAT DO NOT INVOLVE NEAR DEATH EXPERIENCES IN THE LAST TEN PAGES. HAVE I WON THE FICTION LOTTERY? Seriously, I couldn't believe it when it happened <i>again</i>. SO PLEASED.<br /><br />Also, I thought Webster was going to die, a la the explosives expert in the last one, so I was pleased when he pulled through.<br /><br />So what does that leave for me not to like? OH YES, the thing that always gives me issues. Roarke.<br /><br />Now, I'm not saying what he did was completely in the wrong, but him talking about compromise kind of made me laugh, because he never does. Or if he does, he does it with ridiculously good grace and is always shown to be in the right. Always. And it's just so tedious. Because to me, he comes off as impossibly high-handed in this one (again, I'll state, sometimes with good reason, but it always seems to be done SO VERY POORLY).<br /><br />And seriously, dude needs to stop putting various medication in his wife's drinks without her consent. I don't care if it's for her own good in the end. THAT IS NEVER OKAY. It is not like she shows up in his office and shuts off the power because he's staying up too late on a deal, or whatever. I get that she gets him involved in the cases, but I'm sorry, the power dynamic between them is just not quite right, and it shows in this one (though in a lot of ways this one is better for it, but it's also worse in a lot of others). And it's not something that can be handwaved away by "Oh but Roarke is so charming and lovely and he loves her so much and just wants what's best for her." Shut up. It would sit better for me if it didn't always feel like Roarke was being portrayed as the more reasonable one, the one who's more logical, and right. And he is. There is the odd page where he isn't, but in the end it always gets turned so that gets played down.<br /><br />Usually this doesn't bother me this much, but it did in this one.<br /><br />This is becoming a situation where I need Roarke to be wrong in the relationship dynamics. Seriously wrong. Try to pull something on her that he shouldn't, and she gets mad and sticks to her guns. And then he just has to stand there in his wrongness and be wrong.<br /><br />I really like the larger world, and sometimes their relationship really works for me. And it did at times in this, but something didn't quite feel right. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2974250384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1106190170360021740">When another cop is murdered, it really gets to detective Eve Dallas. Add to the fact that the murder was utterly brutal makes Eve work even harder. Eve's intense investigation leads her to a private club called Purgatory. Truly, no one wants membership in this club! Everyone is judged based on their actions and after such, receive a horrendous punishment. <br/><br/>As always in this story, Eve's husband Roarke plays a big role in this current case. Not only is Roarke involved, but Eve's friend Mavis even</span>
  <span id="freeText1106190170360021740" style="display:none">When another cop is murdered, it really gets to detective Eve Dallas. Add to the fact that the murder was utterly brutal makes Eve work even harder. Eve's intense investigation leads her to a private club called Purgatory. Truly, no one wants membership in this club! Everyone is judged based on their actions and after such, receive a horrendous punishment. <br /><br />As always in this story, Eve's husband Roarke plays a big role in this current case. Not only is Roarke involved, but Eve's friend Mavis even steps in to help Eve. The drama and intrigue was intense in this story, as in all of the previous ones I have enjoyed reading. There is no shortage of murders, so Eve really steps up to the game, as always.<br /><br />My TBR has been threatening to riot, so unfortunately I missed my monthly read on the In Death series in October. I am looking forward to getting my hands on the next book in the series, Betrayal in Death, as soon as I can.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o6F2jFZWd3dYnRPydASZ7OF5f8XsY+Zt5zbkzDHdcMprzNEm/Mb8ZmMa/0UspYPQpvvOb3lUSnclNpW/NqEQOw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('75clBTzfhzsJTMZolflvNHXvXCaVYiWo0Roa32LcHnwn+oKvlk8MKjLLKt/NWHUIMm3tjABVibITGmusZaB+jQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9944716315596423365">J.D. Robb is the author of the #1 New York Times bestselling In Death series and the pseudonym for #1 New York Times bestselling author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a>. The futuristic suspense series stars Eve Dallas, a New York City police lieutenant with a dark past. Initially conceived as a trilogy, readers clamored for more of Eve and the mysterious Roarke. Shadows in Death(St. Martin's Press, September 2020) is</span>
  <span id="freeText9944716315596423365" style="display:none">J.D. Robb is the author of the #1 New York Times bestselling In Death series and the pseudonym for #1 New York Times bestselling author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a>. The futuristic suspense series stars Eve Dallas, a New York City police lieutenant with a dark past. Initially conceived as a trilogy, readers clamored for more of Eve and the mysterious Roarke. Shadows in Death(St. Martin's Press, September 2020) is the 51st entry in the series.</span>
